
   Message Format
  ----------------

  Message #1 of 8176 <"- ASCII Signiture Rebuilt"|"- ASCII Signiture As-Is">*

  <Subject>

  <Date/Time>

  <Person & email address>

  <2 blank separator lines then...>

  <Message - "As-Is">

  <2 blank lines then @'s as divider line>


  * ASCII signitures have been rebuilt where possible.
    Unfortunately Yahoo store messages in a way which means more than 1 space
    is stored as just 1 space. Viewing the message source, and then trying to
    view HTML source in Firefox didn't make any difference.
    Where I have been unable to rebuild the ASCII signitures I have simply put
    "ASCII Signiture As-Is" by the message number.

    Thanks to Andrew Allen for preserving Peter Cahill's ASCII signiture for
    me (see message 1613) in November 1998.

    Thanks to Michael Cox, as I was able to cross-reference some emails from
    the Onelist archives with ones posted to the Yahoo one to reinstate email
    addresses that Yahoo has discarded, and rebuild some ASCII signitures.


   Message From Archivist
  ------------------------

   I hope everyone enjoys reading the messages and appreciates me archiving
   them. It took hours of work to get all the info into this file and then 
   rebuild the ASCII signitures as best as I could.
   Don't forget to join, or atleast visit, the Yahoo! AMOS-LIST group:

     http://groups.yahoo.com/group/amos-list


          - Andrew D. Burton, September 2007
            aliensrcooluk@yahoo.co.uk

	Message #459 of 8175 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

AMOS Future + ICQ

Wed Dec 31, 1969 11:59 pm
"Alastair Murray" <malcolm.murray@virgin.net>


Just to add myself to he ICQ database:
Alastair Murray, Muzza, 15173722

And as for AMOS future.
Great work guys! The future looks great!
As for examples on the AMOS update CD. I've done TONS of AMOS stuff as
you can see on my webpage. I'd be quite happy to contirbute both full
games/programs as well as example code. Mail me if you're interested.

As for AMOS NG. Sounds great. I think its just what we need too. I was
getting worried about how AMOS was going to be unuseable in the near
future.

One thing, I notice some other people have voiced concerned about this
too. That is about compatability with current AMOS programs.
I can fully understand that a lot of things will have to be done quite
differently but will keep as close as possible to current AMOS syntax?

Hmmm.. how about a code convertor? Input your AMOS Pro source code in
ASCII and out comes the AMOS NG equivilent. Of course you could then
go through it and make all the necassary optimisations that AMOS NG
would have. Thats the sort of thing I could do myself actually.

Anyway, great work. Please keep us updated as to how progress goes.

-Murray

	Message #463 of 8175 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

More Amos Infos

Sat Aug 1, 1998 8:07 pm
Pietro Ghizzoni <ghizzo@agonet.it>


Hi!

Due to the several messages about the Amos future, i'll reply to all the
questions here:

1- i'm sorry... i've not mentioned this before, but obviously the upgrade will
be available on floppy disks too. (lite version). Anyway a CD is a must for
the full version.... I've a Zip drive, so on request, i can release a Zip
upgrade :)

2- Amos NG is written in C++ but the commands syntax is amos-like... for the
advanced users structured variables, declarations, and tag lists will be
available. For the basic users, all the standard basic functions are
available.
I'm sorry, but you can't directly import your Amos sources, since the
commands are similar but not equal.

3- The AMOS NG editor will be good as the amos one. Anyway you can use your
favourite text editor like GoldEd or CygnusEd.

4- In the CD upgrade is present a new set of Arexx scripts wich allows you to
program in Amos in a more amiga-like way like the other compilers. Now you can
use GoldEd (.. or CygnusEd) and its adavanced features to write your programs,
and trough Arexx you can call the stand-alone amos compiler, and compile your
programs like the others professional C compilers.

5- Soon a new remaked version of The AMOS Factory homepage will be available,
and a new important AMOS project will start. Surprise, surprise :) For this
you have to wait again some days! hehehe.... in this period i was in silence,
but working!


--


Bye!


                                     !!!

   |            Team AMIGA                          \/// 18MB - CD4x    |

for newer machines that it barely should only be used on new machines. New -

touched, but 1.3 machines WAS covered by the original Amos, and you may still

	Message #473 of 8175 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

CBATNAM - Update 3/8/98

Thu Jan 1, 1970 7:59 am
(Keith Hill) <Braneloc@mirex.demon.co.uk>


Well, first of all, to those who are in the know, my car got stolen on
wednesday. ..the update is, the police recovered it, completely intact
with contents unmoved(!) today ! I was as shocked to find it intgact as
I was to lose it in the first place. (Except I was a lot more pleased)

Second...

To all who have contributed to the CBATNAM project, I still need some
things from you, and this means **ALL** of you. You know who you are.
This includes everyne who wrote ANYTHING, or submitted ANY graphics, or
ANY sound, even if it was not used in the final version.

        One:    A "Men In Black" style photo of you, in any format.
        Two:    One or two lines describing yourself in text format for
                the credits.

Send both to:
        bubba@mirex.demon.co.uk

Note, the picture can be in ANY format, I don't care, jpg is best. If
you can't send a picture in digital format, a physical photo can be
returned. If you have not got a black suit, wear the closest you can
get. If you havn't got the shades, wear the closest you can get - but
expect your suit and glasses to be darkened on the final pic. Don't
worry, you'll get to approve it b4 release.

This is now URGENT.... Send as soon as possible. To the people who
have already send the piccies, thankx, but you are very much in the
minority.

....if everyone contributes, it works, if someone misses out, it looks
bad for the rest of us..

Re: AMOS Future

Thu Jan 1, 1970 7:59 am
(Keith Hill) <Braneloc@mirex.demon.co.uk>


> > As for AMOS NG. Sounds great. I think its just what we need too. I was
> > getting worried about how AMOS was going to be unuseable in the near
> > future.

I think the main thing that concerns me, is the new programs I am developing,
rather than converting the old ones. Converting would be nice, however.

Do I wait for Amos NG, do I use AmosPro today, do I use Blitz today, do I
HiSoft today, or do I buy something for the peecee ?

Unfortunately, I am not 100% happy with ANY programming language that is
around today. There just isn't enough damn flexibility.



...as soon as a kernel is available, I am available for development or
testing work. I have an advanced project that needs writing, and needs
a decent machine to run on.

way to the planet.
Hang Glider - flight sim where Cap'n Bubba pilots his hang glider to the
surface of the planet.
Planet Attack - space harrier style where Cap'n Bubba fights the nasty aliens
on the planet.
The Gates Of Doom - tekken style fighting game where Cap'n Bubba faces the
toughest aliens in the planet.
Bubba's Bubbles - pang style quick level to gain extra points whenever the
Cap'n starts hallucinating.

Keith is any indication, the final game will be about 6 megs. We're hoping for
distribution by Mush. There will be a REAL manual, not just on-disk, and we

monitors. One for CyberGFX-displays and one for PAL-displays (eg. AMOS)

	Message #490 of 8175 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: hm

Tue Aug 4, 1998 4:09 pm
"Scooter D. Matott sXe" <sdmatott@midway.uchicago.edu>


>
> In a drawing with about 50 areas, each with a different colour and
> with different irregular shapes, how is it possibile to find each area with
> a mouseclick while pointing to that area?

Piece of cake, use the point command to figure out which colour is
beneath the mouse and then you know which area it's pointing to.
So:
x=screen(x mouse)
y=screen(y mouse)
_colour = Point(x, y)
I'm not sure about the screen syntax but basically just be sure to use the
x and y SCREEN cordinates of the mouse as opposed to the x and y HARDWARE
cordinates which is wahy x mouse, y mouse give you.
Does this make sense? By making every area have it's own colour
you've really made it pretty easy on yourself, of course you're using 64
ehb mode and not HAM to get 50 colours right?

        Scooter d sXe

	Message #491 of 8175 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Setting the record straight

Tue Aug 4, 1998 5:23 pm
"Mr. Giark To You" <giark@hicksville.ddns.org>


Recently, I've been talking with Peter Cahill about TGE. It's the extension
with fast bobs, AGA/RTG, CDDA, the whole nine yards. It uses internal code for
iconify. It uses ptreplay.library for pt commands. It uses GMS for all graphic
commands and CDDA.

Contrary to rumour, I am NOT trying to stop production of TGE. I have no
problem with TGE and, if you are willing to pay the price, it will do all the
things you want it to do.

What do I mean, "pay the price"? GMS, the external `heart' of TGE, has a very
nasty licensing agreement. It's one I do not agree to, and, because of that, I
do not use GMS. I will, however, use TGE for the non-GMS commands.

This is not a message to trash TGE, Peter, GMS or its programmer. This message
is a clarification of why I, personally, alone, on my own, will not use GMS.

For the purposes of this message, I am speaking about creating a game/app
using GMS graphics. The program under consideration would be released as
shareware. If you never plan to release anything as shareware, but only as
freeware, the money argument does not apply to you, though the other licensing
requirements may be of interest.

GMS is a collection of programming tools, to put it simply. It handles AGA/RTG
graphics and CDDA, among other things. It requires libs, modules and prefs to
be on the machine running the GMS-based program. They can all be in one
directory, but still, users have to have them to run the game you have
created, which means you have to either distribute the GMS package with your
creation or point the purchaser to dev/misc/GMS_User.lha on aminet.

From the GMS agreement:
"DEVELOPERS LICENSE. Authors of GMS programs must obtain an official license
before public distribution of said programs. Failure to obtain a license may
impede certain penalties as outlined in the licensing agreement file."

Meaning you have to ask permission to release your game. You wrote the code.
You wrote the music. You made the samples. You drew the graphics. You came up
with the whole idea. Now ask someone else for permission to release it. Does
that bother you at all?

From the GMS agreement:
"The following table illustrates how much you will have to pay for a license
when you want to release a single game."

Each game/app. If you write a game, you pay him. If you write another, you pay
him AGAIN! How many times should you have to pay for the same commands?

From the GMS agreement:
"`The cost of your game' is defined by the amount of money that a consumer has
to pay to buy it. For example, if it costs me $10US to buy your program, your
license will cost $20US."

Which begs the question, how high will you jack your prices up to offset the
cost of this continuing license?

From the GMS agreement:
"Once you have your license you can sell your game for as long as you like,
and are also allowed to distribute the GMS binaries with it. In the above
case, the license cost would be recovered after selling just 2 copies of the
program."

Which means you have to sell at least three copies before you, the author, the
one who did all the work for that game, sees ANY profit. The argument can be
made that the GMS author did a lot of work, too. Agreed, he did. Once. So, I
should pay him, over and over again? That is not an equitable solution. He
wrote the graphic routines. He didn't write my game.

From the GMS agreement:
"If you release more than one game in a year, your license fees can be lowered
(e-mail for details)."

But you will still be paying again and again for the same commands. The
argument has been put forth that you do the same thing when you buy AMOS. The
thing is, you don't have to send Europress money again each time you release a
game. If GMS was a one-time price, that would be fine, but it isn't. It's a
scheme to get the author of GMS cash for doing nothing. Would you have bought
AMOS if you had to pay more money each time you released a program?

Did you buy AMOS 3D? Do you pay more money every time you release a 3D game?
Did you register AmCAF? Do you have to send more money to the author for every
program you release using AmCAF? No? Hmm. Very interesting.

From the GMS agreement:
"Here is the table:
+-------------------+--------------+
| Program Cost (US) | License (US) |
+-------------------+--------------+
|     $0 -  2.99    =     FREE     |
|     $3 - 13.99    =     $20      |
|    $14 - 18.99    =     $30      |
|    $19 - 23.99    =     $40      |
|    $24 - 29.99    =     $60      |
|    $30 - 34.99    =     $80      |
|    $35 - 39.99    =     $120     |
|    $40+           =     $200+    |
+----------------------------------+"

If I charge $40, it will COST me $200 to release my own work? That doesn't
come close to "the license cost would be recovered after selling just 2 copies
of the program", now, does it?

From the GMS agreement:
"The good news is that freeware licenses are available at no charge...you
still must write in and ask for a license, so that I can put you on the
registered page."

So, I still have to ask for permission to release my own work.

From the GMS agreement:
"If you release a sequel to your game (e.g. `Super Tetris II') you will need
to renew your license.  Major revisions (e.g.  V2.0) also require new
licenses.  Minor revisions (e.g. V2.1), bug fixes, and patches do not require
you to re-license your game."

He's really covering all the angles, isn't he?

From the GMS agreement:
"You should be able to recover your license cost after selling only 2 to 4
games."

Except in the examples in his chart, where it could take as many as five
copies.

From the GMS agreement:
"Keep in mind that all license fees go towards the continuation of the
project, so by paying the fees you can ensure that GMS has a good future."

Maybe so. Still, sounds almost like a government inspired plan.

From the GMS agreement:
"If you release a game without a license you will face some penalties. It not
only damages the project, but moves it closer to the PC (I have one sitting on
my desk)."

Well. `If you don't give me money, I'm gonna go play with the PC boys.' I can
not tell you how many `faithful' amiga users spout this crap at the drop of a
hat. If you're just in it for the money, you probably should go play with the
PC boys. Who cares about integrity, right?

From the GMS agreement:
"We will also run a list of people that are found to have not paid for
licenses. Since the list is publicly available, it may be e-mailed to other
web pages and newsgroups for posting. To be fair to you, we give up to 2 weeks
notice if you haven't paid the license fee. After that, you go on the list. If
you break the rules and want to rectify your mistake, you can be pulled from
the list by paying for the license plus another 20% for the trouble you
caused."

How does that sound to you? Are you ready to rush out and get GMS? It makes me
feel all warm and fuzzy, that's for sure.

Don't send me giant responses to this letter, touting the wonders of GMS. I
don't care. The licensing agreement (slavery) does not appeal to me.

Granted, this isn't the whole of the licensing text. Rest assured that I did
not cut out any of the `good points', nor did I remove text to make my point.
You can read them for yourself, but be advised, the licensing agreement is
conspicuously absent from the GMS_User.lha archive. The developer archive does
contain the licensing agreement, if you want to read up on it.

In conclusion, I am not telling you to avoid GMS. I am not telling you to
avoid TGE. I am not slagging Peter or the GMS author. I AM pointing out the
pitfalls/costs of using GMS. Use if if you want. I won't and the reasons I
won't are abundantly clear.

I will not reply to any messages about GMS. I am not trying to start a
flamefest/argument/debate. This is my opinion. It is not my intention to
influence your decision, only to make you aware of the facts.

Well met and godspeed,
                      Giark
                                             ICQ 12235820
                                       giark@hicksville.ddns.org
                                http://www.hicksville.ddns.org/~erotica/
                            .----------------------------------------------.
                            |      ______  ______    _____                 |
                            |     / ____/ / __  /   / ___ \ Makers of      |
                            |    / /__   / /_/ /   / /  / / SoloTrek II    |

	Message #496 of 8175 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Various things

Wed Dec 31, 1969 11:59 pm
"Alastair Murray" <malcolm.murray@virgin.net>


> I think the main thing that concerns me, is the new programs I am developing,
> rather than converting the old ones. Converting would be nice, however.
>
> Do I wait for Amos NG, do I use AmosPro today, do I use Blitz today, do I
> HiSoft today, or do I buy something for the peecee ?

I had a more of a go with Blitz recently and was quite suprised to find
that it had far more bugs and problems than AMOS ever had. It doesn't
support many basic things (such as proper shape clipping) and is a pain to
use. Even procedures/functions are very poorly implemented. How did it ever
get popular?
It seems apart from a few better structures there is only the fact that the
screens are OS friendly that gives it any advantage over AMOS.
Perhaps a slight speed advantage too but its not as much as some people
make out.

> Unfortunately, I am not 100% happy with ANY programming language that is
> around today. There just isn't enough damn flexibility.

I agree. AMOS has screen problems and lack of updates (soon to be changed
of course!), Blitz is just full of all sorts of problems and then there is
nothing between them and C (at least for developing games).
I don't have the time to code in C (although I am slowly doing a bit) but
get annoyed at the screen problems with AMOS.

-----

> As for GFX cards, you'd need one that automatically convert standard
> Amiga displays to high sync ones. (eg, one with a fliker fixer). I'm not
> sure if that'll work 100% though.

Problem is that the Bvision which is what I'm going to get does not have a
scan doubler....

-----

> Wasn't there a tutorial on a Disk Mag somewhere. Anyway, I've taught
> myself
> AMOS 3D by trial and error, and I must say its not as good as it shoud
> have
> been, its really hard to use. May as well wait for a new version.

AMOS 3D certainly could have been much better, however it is possible to
get some reasonable results out of it once you get to know it well.
My main problem is the terrible object editor program. It is so inprecise.

Anyway, check out Star Fighter from Geosync for a good example.
Also just the other day there was an AMOS 3D example put on AMINET. It is
of a flight simulator and although the graphics are simple it does go
pretty fast and smoothly and is a good example of creating a whole 3D
world.

I found that games in space are not too hard to do because you can get away
with not that many objects, however cames on land are much harder because
they require scenery. They can be done though!

-----

One last thing. I'm really starting to worry how I'll be able to work on
AMOS once I get my GFX card and monitor. I can't take a TV and monitor
everywhere with me.
I understand that the updated version of AMOS will have provisions for a
screen friendly editor. How long until this is ready? Is there no fix I
could get to do this? Also, will this new version of AMOS have more OS
friendly screens (in game screens) or will that have to wait until AMOS NG?

Thanks,
-Murray

	Message #497 of 8175 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

TGE or not TGE

Sat Aug 1, 1998 5:02 pm
Peter Cahill <cahill4@iol.ie>


Hello,

As some of you know, games that are written using TGE may cost,
depending on if there freeware or not. This cost is due to TGE
using GMS, which I find it worth the extra cost.

GMS stands for 'Games Master System', it is a extremly fast
system, coded in a mixture of C and Asm. GMS does graphics
better than amos in from the fact that in amos on my 030@50
I can have about 60 bobs(8x8), and If I move 1 Its as jerky
as hell, but, with GMS on my 030@50, I have had about 300+
8x8 bobs on a higher res screen AND ALL the bobs were changeing
sizes and ALL moving at diffrent speeds, and they were nice
and Smooootthhh. GMS supports ECS,AGA and Gfx card modes.

The costs of 'GMS' are around 2/3 times the price of your game
if your game is free, then you dont need to pay anything. you
*DONT* need to mention GMS anywhere in your code And I honestly
think that if your game isnt gonna sell more than 2 copies then
you should release it as freeware.

The reason for this mail is that one person in particular
(hi giark) has been at me about it costing for quite some
time. Saying that he wont use it because 'He wont give
credit of his work to anyone else'. After *MANY*
2 and 3 hour IRC sessions with this person I have decided
to settle this with a survey, of how many people actually
want TGE.

And Id like to see how many people wouldnt like TGE and
'wouldnt pay $5 for a GMS lisence for a shareware or
commercial game of theres' and 'wouldnt give any credit
of there creativity to someone else, as the author of
GMS didnt use creativity in making GMS' and 'wont pay
GMS because he didnt pay for his AmigaOperatingSystem'
but I always thaught that you paid for the OS when
buying a amiga, maybe Im wrong.

So could anyone who wants TGE to continue please
reply to this mail asap.

Also anyone who wants TGE to cease if its going to
cost ANYTHING, please reply also.

thanks,
--

> So could anyone who wants TGE to continue please

Perhaps I am a poor sample of the population at large, but I for
one never aim to make money off anything I write in amos. I code for the
fun and thrill of unleashing my imagination in a way only a groovy
computer like the amiga could let me.
So bottom line is this, if TGE will help my convert my ideas to
reality without alot of frustration then of course I'd want to use it, and
if it proved proffesional enough a package (ie stable, well documented) I
wouldn't mind paying to use it.

	Message #505 of 8175 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: hm

Tue Aug 4, 1998 11:23 pm
Nikola Smolenski <smolensk@EUnet.yu>


On 02-Avg-91, Hakan Venderlof wrote:

HV> In a drawing with about 50 areas, each with a different colour and
HV> with different irregular shapes, how is it possibile to find each area
with
HV> a mouseclick while pointing to that area?

I think that the best and easiest way is one Scooter told you about, but if
you are
using 50 different colors only because of finding area, I would suggest you
method with which you can use only one color, if you want:

1) Create array which will hold X and Y coordinates of one point in the
middle of each area.
2) When mouse is clicked, use Paint command on mouse coordinates (of
course, translate hardware coordinates into screen coordinates), with color
which doesn't belong to any area.
3) Use Point() for every point in your array to find which point has that
color.
4) That's your area. Now just paint it again in the old color. If you use
color
which have diferent index, but same value as original, this wouldn't be
visible by the user (or, I guess, player ;) .

Regards
--

Just a quick gripe to all those on the list, Ive been away from this list for
almost a year and I see things just havent changed, capn bubba still not
finished, arguing between blitz and amos and also the wishful thinking that
someone somewhere is going to market an enhanced version of AMOS, for me I wish
the latter was going to happen, but unfortunately the reality of it all is NOT
LIKELY, well not for the current Amiga architecture that we all know and love,
so just like all the other Amiga owners, we will have to wait and see what
transpires (if anything) of the future platform and its development tools, so
until then we use what we have and play around on this fun but old looking
machine.

I say forget writing games, forget writing 3rd rate extensions for Amos Pro,
develop something that displays the current and high-end amiga technology,
develop multimedia applications, theres a far greater future in that, after all,
why did we all buy an amiga in the first place? graphics and sound !!!

Dave Paterson

	Message #519 of 8175

Re: Copyright

Wed Aug 5, 1998 2:13 pm
"Dave Paterson" <y2guru@sprynet.com>


Hi,

If you are that concerned about copyright, do this:-

Copy all your material to floppy
Place in an envelope
Mail it to yourself
Store away for safe keeping, DO NOT OPEN

What does this prove?

Well, the post office will date stamp your package and any copyright problems
that could occur will be avoided as you have proof that your material was
produced prior to the date on the envelope

Dave

Peter Cahill <cahill4@iol.ie>


On 04-Aug-98, Mr. Giark To You wrote:

Hi

>Recently, I've been talking with Peter Cahill about TGE. It's the extension
>with fast bobs, AGA/RTG, CDDA, the whole nine yards. It uses internal code for
>iconify. It uses ptreplay.library for pt commands. It uses GMS for all graphic
>commands and CDDA.

No, CDDA is internal in TGE as are quite a few other features that you left out,
like the encryption for example.

>GMS is a collection of programming tools, to put it simply. It handles AGA/RTG
>graphics and CDDA, among other things. It requires libs, modules and prefs to
>be on the machine running the GMS-based program. They can all be in one
>directory, but still, users have to have them to run the game you have
>created, which means you have to either distribute the GMS package with your
>creation or point the purchaser to dev/misc/GMS_User.lha on aminet.

No, I have provided methods of suppling a 'small' version of GMS, this
DOES make your code about 60-70k bigger, but enables all GMS features. Whats
missing is just the docs, prefs and some other extras.

>Which means you have to sell at least three copies before you, the author, the
>one who did all the work for that game, sees ANY profit. The argument can be
>made that the GMS author did a lot of work, too. Agreed, he did. Once. So, I
>should pay him, over and over again? That is not an equitable solution. He
>wrote the graphic routines. He didn't write my game.

He wrote more than 'just the graphic routines' and if you release a game
which wont sell more than 2 copys it should be freeware.

>>From the GMS agreement:
>"The good news is that freeware licenses are available at no charge...you
>still must write in and ask for a license, so that I can put you on the
>registered page."

>So, I still have to ask for permission to release my own work.

No, wrong again, you make it sound much worse than it is, all he
asked was that you let him know that you want a lisence, and YOU
WILL GET IT, its not a maybe.

>He's really covering all the angles, isn't he?

Thats cos guys like you atack at all angles dont you ?

>Don't send me giant responses to this letter, touting the wonders of GMS. I
>don't care. The licensing agreement (slavery) does not appeal to me.

like'and if you dont pay the lisence I'll kill you' in that somewhere ?!?

>Granted, this isn't the whole of the licensing text. Rest assured that I did

TGE/GMS

Wed Dec 31, 1969 11:59 pm
"Alastair Murray" <malcolm.murray@virgin.net>


I think the GMS fees are fair and I will certainly use TGE.
The one thing I think is unfair is that of user registration but that
isn't too bad either.

Basically, if you are making any program that is free, there's nothing
to worry about and you can use all the enhanced features for nothing.

If you are producing software that you charge for then you have to pay
the price of about two registations. Thats nothing. Its not like you
will be knowcking up games every month (if you are then they are most
likely not of good enough quality to charge money anyway) so you don't
have to pay much at all.

-Murray

3D-Ground Scroll with Rainbows

Wed Aug 5, 1998 9:22 pm
"Scooter D. Matott sXe" <sdmatott@midway.uchicago.edu>


Howdy,
Last night I got a bright idea and drafted up some code that uses
a rainbow to create a scrolling ground effect ala Space Harrier or 3D
world runner. It's a simple effect and I've seen it down a 1,000 times
with colour shifting, but this routine's genuis is that it eats up only
colour register thanks to the use of rainbows. Also it's easy to control
the speed/smoothness of it all and I get 60 fps off my loop. Anyway if
anybody's interested in how to do such a thing drop me a line.

                        Thanks,
                                Scott Matott sXe
PS
        Has anybody out there ever gotten more than one Rainbow to appear
on the same scan line, the manual says it can be done just not easily.
Still it I could do it this routine could prove much, much more powerful.

	Message #539 of 8175

Re: off-topic: CDDA

Wed Aug 5, 1998 11:20 pm
Richard Griffith <ragriffi@sprynet.com>


On 05-Aug-98, Rune J. Keller wrote:
>From: "Rune J. Keller" <keller@vip.cybercity.dk>

>I'm trying to read the digital audio from a cd (NOT to sample it!) for
>later
>conversion to mp3. No matter what program I use, I can't get the job
>done. Has
>anyone tried the same? Which program works and who do you use it?

I use AsimCDFS, it works like a charm. However, not all cd-rom
drives can read CDDA as data. Older drives (or older designs)
won't do it. It was not a technical limitation, it was the Phillips
CD technology license that forbid the direct export of CDDA as
a digital stream.

-Richard

Re: Copyright

Wed Aug 5, 1998 8:24 pm
Andy Gibson <andy@agasinc.demon.co.uk>


This message arrived in my mail box:
Date: Wednesday 05-Aug-98
Time: 13:04:12
Name: Declan Gorman
Subject: [amos-list] Copyright
So here's a reply...

Hi there Declan,

> Is it enough to put "(c) Declan Gorman" within my program
and documentation
> to copyright my program or is there something else I should
be doing?

For starters, do NOT put (c)!!! use the Copyright symbol
which is © (Alt & E together on GB keymap). (c) isn't really
the Copyright sign! It is not legally accepted as far as I
recall! Or am I wrong on this? - Anyone?

Anything you produce is automatically copyrighted to you. If
you want to be doubly sure, post a copy of your work to
yourself 9don't open it though) and keep it safe. You could
also post a copy to your solicitor (like, yeah, we all have
one :) for double safety :-)

If it's copyright rules you need for your dox, isn't there a
standard set somewhere?

	Message #549 of 8175 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

To be or not TGE.

Thu Aug 6, 1998 5:37 am
"Adam Parrott" <parrottsoft@usa.net>


On the issue of TGE:

I'd have to say that it sounds like a welcome addition to any AMOS user or
developer (just as both AMCAF and GUI have been). The fact that it uses GMS
as part of it's infrastructure isn't a problem with me, and I would have to
agree with the others who have stated their freeware/charge money solution.
(If you don't sell more than a few copies, then it's probably freeware).

I can't say that the restrictions imposed by GMS are TOTALLY unreasonable
(the fees namely), although I can say that I don't really like them. In a
half-sense, it sounds like the author of GMS is just trying to make a few
(sometimes more than) bucks off of his program. But as Andy Gibson said,
"if you don't want to pay, then don't use it". I would have to agree. If I
choose not to use it, I'm sure I can find something else to substitute.

I do promote Peter in his efforts, and I will encourage him to continue.
This project has been a long time in coming, and although I may need TGE as
badly as some of my fellow developers, I will welcome it's timely arrival.

PS: I can understand Giark's perspective, but I must say it came off VERY
half-cocked. Although I might support a few of his points, he sounded like
the perfect example for the next "Lazy Programmer Poster Child".

Renamer

Thu Aug 6, 1998 4:19 pm
"Mr. Giark To You" <giark@hicksville.ddns.org>


A friend on IRC asked for a program to rename an entire directory. The result
is Renamer (FBN-Rnam.lha). It can be found on aminet. What it does it let you
pick a directory, root name and base number, after which it goes through the
directory and renames every file, retaining the extension (last four
characters).

	Message #560 of 8175 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

3-D Ground Scroll Code Idea

Thu Aug 6, 1998 4:39 pm
"Scooter D. Matott sXe" <sdmatott@midway.uchicago.edu>


Wow!
I guess I didn't really expect much interest in this one, well now
that the spot light is on I just hope the idea is actually a good one,
worked like a charm for me but who knows...

Ok here's an outline of what i did, oh and the ground it produces
is sadly not a checker pattern like Space Harrier (This could easily be
done though if only we could put two rainbows on the same scan line)
But insteadis the same thing w/o the checkering so just a scroll of two
bars of colour.
Anyway, here's the idea:

Pre-program a simple 3-D scroll, read out this info and use the
Rain command to make


Here's a rough sketch of how I did it:

First I used Dpaint IV in this way
I drew up a red big square then I cut it out and
stuck a White copy of it onit's top, making a two colour
rectangle wplit down the middle (got the idea)

Then I set Frames to 100 and used perspective mode and the
Move requester with Fill option to make a scrolling ground
(Have you all done this before, if not I can tell you how)
I also deleted the top garbage looking part of the scroll
(about the first 18 lines of it) Leaving a scroll that
was about 9 'bars' of colour deep. Does that make sense?

Ok then I saved each frame into Ram numbered 1 to 50.

Then I set up a loop in amos to load each frame and
starting from the bottom of the screen move up using
the Point command, grabb the y cordinate at each change in
colour.

So I ended up with 9 numbers telling me where
each "bar" in the scroll started. As well I could
find the where each bar ended by taking the starting point
of the next bar and subtracting one. (The last bar always
has the same end point which is the top y cord. of my scroll)

I copied all of these starting points into a Memory bank
using poke as the are all numbers less than 256.

I did the same for each frame, copying them all into
a bank of size 50*9 (50 frames, nine bars per frame)

Do you get the idea yet? Now I have a memory bank which
tells me where to start and finish drawing horizontal
bars of colour to produce a scrolling ground.

So from there the rest is simple, but the rainbow part is what
makes it all worth while

I just set up a loop to read these start and end points
back out and then draw the bars of colour into the Rainbow
which is fast, fast, fast!

So the code looks like this

First set up a Rainbow 200 scan lines big with nothing in it
then display it (again 200 lines big, or 255 is it for Pal?)

I used Colour register 2 for my rainbow, so then clear
the screen in colour 2.

Use the Rain command to black out the part of the Rainbow you
won't use, (So my Scroll is about 82 pixels high, so I used rain
to stick $000 into the first 118 scan lines of the rainbow)

Now use a loop like this

For FRAME=0 to 49
For _BAR=0 to 8
Rem Get start and End for colour Bar
_START = Fetch_Bar_Start[_BAR,FRAME]
If _BAR=8 Then _END=118
Else _END =Fetch_Bar_Start[_BAR,FRAME] - 1
Rem Pick a Colour for the Bar, Notice for a looping scroll you will
Rem to Do a little more work here
If _BAR mod 2 = 0 Then _COLOUR=4096
Else _COLOUR=3000

rem Now a loop that puts the right colour in each scan line of the bar
rem you must go from _end to _start because of Amos's cordinate system
rem Which has 0 on the top of the screen and 199 on the bottom.
For Z=_END to _START
Rain(0,Z)=_COLOUR
Next Z
Next _BAR
Next FRAME

Does any of this make any sense? The idea is simply to preprogram
your scroll and then use rainbow to display it, the genius is that it uses
only one colour and it has serious potential.
Because the whole thing is stored as a list of Frames you can move
at any speed you want, 4 Frames at a time, 1 Frame at a time, ect. ect.
You can also move backwards easily too. Plus at 50 frames the resolution
of the scroll is very good and everyhting looks very smooth no matter what
speed you go at. The only caveat to all this is to make sure to handle
things right in looping from the last frame back to the first (ie careful
with FRAME=54 or FRAME=-2)
There are no restrictions on what colour the Bars can be, and by
using another memory bank as a Map it'd be very easy to program 'levels'
to scroll through, with gaps in the ground (ie black Bars) and baddies
waiting at certain bars, ect. ect.
My plan is not to have the entire ground scroll but instead just
use a narrow strip down the center of the screen. This looks alot
better, as I have the strip tilted in perspective giving sort of
guidelines to your eyes for the depth of the whole thing.

Anyway, hope this makes sense, any questions ask away, I have the
code, wish I'd brought it with me, but I'm off on break til next thursday
so it maybe awhile before I can answer you. Still I'll be around for a
while today.
                        Thanks,
                                Scott Matott sXe

	Message #566 of 8175 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Games programming

Wed Dec 31, 1969 11:59 pm
"Alastair Murray" <malcolm.murray@virgin.net>


> if you're gonna write games, do it on a
> platform where the hardware is consistent, what about the sony playstation
> development machine,

They are extremly hard to get hold of and on top of that you need a good PC
to connect it too.
We are using AMIGAs because either we don't have/can't afford PC's or more
likely because we don't like them.

I don't quite understand you, you make it sound like we are trying to
produce commerical games. It can be done (and has been many times) but most
people here are just making them for fun.

Even if we did start programming a Playstation, the game quality would not
improve very much because we don't have access to professional equipment.
You need teams of artists, programmers and top quality 3D
scanning/rendering hardware to make most good modern games.

> you get all the tools and if the game is any good you
> get Sonys backing!!!! you cant go wrong there, games in Amos look bad,
> regardless of the extensions, they're just plain slow and 8bit looking, the

If they are 8 bit looking that is because we don't have the backing of
professional game artists. It would be no different if we moved to a
playstation.
You make it sound as though the graphics draw themselves.

As for speed. A playstation is obviously faster but the sort of games that
we write anyway would make no impact on that platform because all the kids
want is flashy 3D graphics and techno music (ok... a stereotype :)

And anyway, I am getting a PPC tommorow and intend to start developing some
games for that. Is it going to look any better than my AMOS stuff? Probably
not. It will run faster (although I am good at optimising AMOS stuff anyway
so don't complain about its speed) and may be able to use higher resolutions
but it won't improve my dire graphics skills!!!

> truth hurts i know, but im just giving you a word of advice as ive been
> developing professionally now for 16 years across many platforms.

Exactly. You're developing professionally. We're not.

I know I could get faster games if I moved over to coding on a PC. I have
tried but for me it takes most of the fun away from it.

Programming on the AMIGA means it is more fun for me (and I do it for fun!)
and it also lets me support my favourite platform in some small way.

You may only be interested in the money side so it obviously better for you
to code on PCs/Playstations but we do it for a hobby.

Now just stop trying to put everyone down doing something they enjoy.

-Murray

	Message #590 of 8175

Amos, Games Programming and General Amiga Stuff

Fri Aug 7, 1998 3:12 am
"Dave Paterson" <y2guru@sprynet.com>


Hello again!!!


Well, now that pretty much everyone on this list has aired their views on my
comments, i just want to re-inforce a few issues:-

1. I wanted feedback on how you feel and how open you all are to change
2. I own 3 amigas of varying size and use them all to test my codes performance
and how they operate
under different memory configurations and hardware setup.
3. I code for fun myself on my A4000 and that includes my own modules and
graphics, even though Im not
the worlds greatest musician or artist.
4. I AM an AMIGA enthusiast and have been since 1986
5. I have also used AMOS since "The Creator" was first released
6. I think very highly of both the AMIGA platform and AMOS, but on the otherhand
Im also disappointed that
after all these years, AMOS has not grown and the compiler hasn't been
re-written
7. Would I write games for the PC, NO WAY !!!

So, there you have it, didn't mean to piss on anyones fires, that was not the
intention. Just remember there are so many people on this list that excel in
varying areas, graphics, sound, coding etc... are these people being used to
their full extent ?

Im as interested as the next person to see some great quality games etc... come
from this group as I know you are all keen, even if no money is involved (which
is not the priority)

Dave Paterson

	Message #606 of 8176 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: GUI

Fri Aug 7, 1998 8:29 pm
Pietro Ghizzoni <ghizzo@agonet.it>


Hello Cox,

On 06-Ago-98, Cox, Michael D wrote: [amos-list] Re: GUI

> From: "Cox, Michael D" <michael.cox@eds.com>
>
> Well, the GUI Path patched amos.library to work with programs using the
> GUI Extension. GUIComp is what you use to compile programs using the
> GUI Extension.
>
> At least I think that is right. I am sure Pietro can explain it better.
> Pietro, perhaps include a list of files needed for GUIExt 1.7 as the 1.7
> and 1.62 archives are different.

Well.... the GUIComp Patch creates a new patched version of your compiler and
related files. It also create a patched verision of the amos.library.. the
gui.library used by the *GUI compiler only.*

The GUI compiler is useful if you want create true WB applications, since it
removes some AMOS problems, like unusefull patches, hacks, and activate the
possibility to run several AMOS programs togheter.


--


Bye!

	Message #618 of 8176 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: is it worth learning amos?

Sun Aug 9, 1998 1:30 am
"Garfield Benjamin" <gbenjam@sosbbs.com>


> Here's the deal:
> I've had AMOS for a long time, but I felt it was dying and pretty much
> useless, plus I didn't know how to program.

Understandable... Europress dropped support and AMOS received
some bad press (from major Amiga mags). However, AMOS is a
fine programming language and that is why loads of people
continue (or come back to) using it.


> I really wanted to learn something, and I was always told it's easier
> to learn to code on a PC... because they don't offer Amiga
> programming classes on my side of Earth.

When the Amiga first came out, many programmers found the
concepts of the OS combined with learning C too much to handle
and thus began the Amiga's reputation as a complicated machine
to program. Obviously, these days we have high level languages
such as AMOS so that "hard-case" rep. is simply no longer true.

I think the best way to learn is to pick up some books and
dive right in. I am a fully self-educated programmer, having never
stepped inside a college in my life (well, I did visit a friend but you
know what I mean).

Just mess around until you have mastered the basics and then
you will be able to move on to more challenging projects.


> So I bought a PC and started taking classes on Visual Basic
> programming. I'm glad I did.. I learned alot of "BASIC" stuff in the
> process. So here are my questions:
> Should I learn Amos Pro 2 or is 3 going to be a whole different
> thing?
> All I have is Amos Pro 2 and the book to Easy Amos.
> Could I learn AP2 with the easy amos book or is it too different?

Use the AMOS version you have... program every day until you
understand exactly what is going on, why it is happening and how
it is being done. Once you have this level of understanding you
will find that you can apply your skill to any language. You see,
all programming is relatively the same... there are always
fundamental elements that must be included in a programming
environment. You might use DISPLAY(), PRINT "", printf(""), puts_,
etc. but the important thing is that there is always a command to
display information on the screen/window.

Currently, I am using DBL at work in a mainframe environment, but
I can easily duplicate my DBL work in AMOS, BLITZ, C/C++, etc. by
relying on the fundamentals... So, master the programming basics.
AMOS is a fantastic tool for doing this and I wish I had something
like AMOS when I started programming (nearly 18 years ago on an
old TI-99/4a - preC64).

In a way, I envy you... you are at the very beginning of your
journey... a time filled with magic and mystery.

Good luck and I hope some of this babbling helps...


             Garfield Benjamin    e-mail:gbenjam@sosbbs.com
                  Website( http://www.sosbbs.com/~gbenjam )

	Message #631 of 8176 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: (no subject)

Mon Aug 10, 1998 9:09 pm
Andrew Crowe <andrewcrowe@enterprise.net>


Hi Everybody,

> From: Hakan Venderlof <grok@flashback.net>

> How is it possible to load variables
> A,B,C into

> Colour Nr,$RGB ?

> I mean like if A=1 B=4 C=6
> then
> Colour Nr,$146

Ah yes, I had to do this when my copy of CRAFT broke, I think this
should
do it:

CR=A*256
CG=B*16
CB=C

Colour Nr,CR+CG+CB.

Of course, its easier to do in craft (craft also has more useful
colour
commands, like 'Pal Set Red' and 'Pal Get Red' etc.)

...keeping in mind that you can't use hex digits. Simply use decimal
equivalents.

	Message #635 of 8176 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: (no subject)

Mon Aug 10, 1998 11:33 pm
"Rune J. Keller" <keller@vip.cybercity.dk>


On 11-Aug-98, Hakan Venderlof wrote:
> I would like to see a code which takes any text and
> converts a given letter to two others like

>>>> ss just an example of course, I would use it
> to convert some swedish letters in som texts...

You create two banks. The first with the original text, the second with the
converted (length of bank1*2). Go through each letter in bank 1 (peek) and
copy it to bank 2 (poke). Except if it is the letter which you want to
convert; then you add two letters (poke, poke) to bank 2.

You could do it with AMCAF commands Bank stretch/shrink aswell, but that tends
to be a bad idea...

--
rune j. keller - sporuplundsvej 105 - dk-8472 sporup - keller@vip.cybercity.dk

	Message #641 of 8176 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: translate

Tue Aug 11, 1998 4:49 pm
"Mr. Giark To You" <giark@hicksville.ddns.org>


On 11-Aug-98, Hakan Venderlof wrote:
>You create two banks. The first with the original text, the second with the
>converted (length of bank1*2). Go through each letter in bank 1 (peek) and
>copy it to bank 2 (poke). Except if it is the letter which you want to
>convert; then you add two letters (poke, poke) to bank 2.
>Sounds interesting...hm..but I've never used peek or poke,
>don't think I can figure how to write this.

Open In 1,"file to translate"
LG=Lof(1)
Reserve As Work 7,LG
Bload "file to translate",7
NG=LG*2
Reserve As Work 8,NG
A=Start(7)
B=A+Length(7)
D=Start(8)
For C=A To B
A$=Peek$(C,1)
If A$="å"
A$="ss"
End If
Poke$ D,A$
D=D+Len(A$)
Next C
E=Start(8)
Bsave "translated file",E To D+1
End

I'm sure there are bugs in this, but it should get you started.

Well met and godspeed,

	Message #642 of 8176 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: (no subject)

Tue Aug 11, 1998 4:55 pm
"Rune J. Keller" <keller@vip.cybercity.dk>


On 11-Aug-98, Hakan Venderlof wrote:
> From: Hakan Venderlof <grok@flashback.net>

> On 10-Aug-98, Rune J. Keller wrote:
>>>> From: "Rune J. Keller" <keller@vip.cybercity.dk>

>>>> On 11-Aug-98, Hakan Venderlof wrote:
>>>>> I would like to see a code which takes any text and
>>>>> converts a given letter to two others like

>>>>>>>> ss just an example of course, I would use it
>>>>> to convert some swedish letters in som texts...

>>>> You create two banks. The first with the original text, the second with
the
>>>> converted (length of bank1*2). Go through each letter in bank 1 (peek)
and
>>>> copy it to bank 2 (poke). Except if it is the letter which you want to
>>>> convert; then you add two letters (poke, poke) to bank 2.

> Sounds interesting...hm..but I've never used peek or poke,
> don't think I can figure how to write this.

Wload "file",10
Reserve as data 11,length(10)*2
d=start(11)

for a=0 to length(10)
b=peek(start(10)+a)
if b=c
rem c being the ascii code of the character to convert
poke d,e
rem e being the ascii code of the first character you want to convert to
poke d+1,f
rem f being the ascii code of the second chracter you want to convert to
d=d+2
else
poke d,b
d=d+1
endif
next

bsave "file2",start(11) to d

Should do the trick. Warning: You are peeking and poking so the computer may
easily crash, if you are doing something wrong!

--
rune j. keller - sporuplundsvej 105 - dk-8472 sporup - keller@vip.cybercity.dk

>>> screens, dual playfield effects & sprites ?

>> Yep It can be done, either use the graphics
>> grabber in HRTmon, or theres a screen snapshot
>> function on aminet which can do amos's screens.

> I too would love to be able to grab Amos screens with ease!

have you tried this, Press Ctrl-C during your program, then
save each screen as an IFF, then load up your paint program, put
it to the max. numbers of colours (24 bit is nice), load the saved
screens as brushes, remap there palette to the pictures, and simply
paste the brushes over each other
(I've done that, but if your screens are different res. then you'll
have to set the paint package to a high res and scale the brushes
yourself). Then reduce the no. of colour to however many you need.

Its not very exact, but it does work.

(Or you could run AmigaUAE which runs AMOS stuff, and grab its screen)


See ya.
--

change 6 letters

Thu Aug 13, 1998 8:04 am
Hakan Venderlof <grok@flashback.net>


Open In 1,"Ram:1"
LG=Lof(1)
Reserve As Work 7,LG
Bload "Ram:1",7
NG=LG*2
Reserve As Work 8,NG
A=Start(7)
B=A+Length(7)
D=Start(8)
For C=A To B
A$=Peek$(C,1)
If A$="k"
A$="aa"
End If
Poke$ D,A$
D=D+Len(A$)
Next C
E=Start(8)
Bsave "Ram:2",E To D+1

Hello...

Thanks...
..this code works fine for changing one letter
in a text.

Is there some smart way to repeat this code so
it will change 6 letters (that is 3 swedish letters in
upper/lowercase)?


--

 greets  grok@flashback.net  (or: grok@online.idg.se)

Compiler?

Thu Aug 13, 1998 8:38 pm
"Mr. Giark To You" <giark@hicksville.ddns.org>


Here's a question that I've always wondered about:

What does the compiler do?

I mean, does it just pick and choose bits of code from extensions as needed?
Could there be a separate program to optimize for different processors after
the program has first been compiled? Can it be modified to do proper version
information? Perhaps have the shell scan through your source for '$VER
progname 2.54 or whatever and use that for the program version? If not, would
anyone be interested in a utility to fix the version number of a program? And,
would adding a bit of info to the version string corrput the program? Right
now, it only has a number, but some programs have the program name and version
number.

	Message #655 of 8176

Sad announcement (fwd) (fwd)

Thu Aug 13, 1998 9:03 pm
jono <jono@enti.demon.co.uk>


*** Forwarded message, originally written by Rick Hodger on 13-Aug-98 ***
*** Forwarded message, originally written by Tony Horgan on 13-Aug-98
at 16:48:55 ***

<fontfamily><param>Geneva</param><smaller>Hello


It is with great regret that I have to inform you that the October
1998
issue of CU Amiga will be the last ever published. CU Amiga Magazine
recently dipped into a state of unprofitability, from which it looked
unlikely to emerge. The decision to close the magazine was taken by
EMAP in light of the magazine's overall financial performance and the
lack of prospects for any immediate or short term recovery.


It is ironic that CU Amiga should close as the world's best selling
Amiga magazine, but recently its financial returns have started to
outweigh its overheads. While it has been customary for costs to be
cut
in order to stave off the closure of magazines, it was decided that CU
Amiga would be laid to rest without suffering the indignities of
having
half its pages removed and the remaineder printed on toilet paper in
black and white. Neither will it be sold off to another company to be
published on a shoe string and run into the ground.


The CU Amiga editorial team were obviously very sorry to hear the news
and would like to pass on their sincere thanks to everyone who has
helped make CU Amiga such a success and so much fun to work on over
its
many years of existence.


Further details can be found on the CU Amiga website:

www.cu-amiga.co.uk


----------


CU Amiga Magazine Closes


FAQ


Q: Why is CU Amiga closing?

A: Because it is no longer making a profit and therefore cannot
continue to be published.


Q: How can the best selling Amiga magazine not make a profit when
other
smaller magazines manage to do it?

A: Smaller magazines have different publishing set-ups, different
costs
and different distribution channels. Many are run at a slight loss or
at break-even by dedicated people as extended hobbies. CU Amiga is
published by a major magazine publishing company (EMAP), and as a
Publicly Limited Company (PLC) EMAP must show its shareholders that it
is making their money work, which means they cannot publish magazines
that make a loss.


Q: Why are costs not cut in order to save the magazine?

A: We feel it is better to leave on a high note than continually
reduce
the size of the magazine, remove the disks, reduce staff and
investment
in the title to keep it going regardless of quality.


Q: Surely though something can be done?

A: We could reduce the magazine to a low quality pamphlet that was
poorly researched and written but then it wouldn't be worth the
£4.50/£5.99 cover price.


Q: Why don't the staff all take a pay cut?

A: Would you do the same?


Q: Why have you lead us to believe the magazine would not close?

A: We never did that. We have always been honest and said that there
would come a time (if things did not pick up) when the magazine would
no longer be profitable. No-one knew when that time would be. Only
very
recently did it become apparent that the time was now.


Q: Is this a ploy to get Amiga users to buy PCs?

A: No. CU Amiga's publisher has no PC magazines anyway.


Q: Will "CU Amiga" be turned into "CU PC"?

A: No.


Q: I have a subscription. How do I get a refund on issues I will not
get?

A: See updated website FAQ for details.


Q: Why isn't the magazine sold to a publisher who can make a profit
from it?

A: Sacrifices would have to be made by any pubilsher that would
compromise the magazine so that it would no longer be the CU Amiga you
currently know.


Q: Will CU Amiga return when the new Super Amiga is released?

A: We hope so, although we cannot make any promises on that one. That
decision will be in the hands of our (ex) publisher (EMAP).


Q: Can I take this opportunity to thank the team for their dedication
to the magazine and the Amiga community?

A: Of course you can. Thank you.


Q: And what about us?

A: Well, there's always Amiga Format (as far as we know at this point
anyway). Nick and Ben will look after you. We really are very sorry to
have to leave you like this. We would all love to go on working on the
magazine well into the future but it's just not possible. One way or
another we'll be around when the Super Amiga surfaces, even though it
most likely won't be a Class of 98 style reunion of the whole team
under the old banner.


Q: So is it time to pack the Amiga away for good?

A: No! Keep on keeping on and we'll see you soon in happier
times.</smaller></fontfamily>



Tony Horgan - Editor, CU Amiga Magazine




*** End of forwarded message ***

	Message #662 of 8176 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: Compiler?

Fri Aug 14, 1998 9:09 am
Nikola Smolenski <smolensk@EUnet.yu>


On 13-Avg-98, Mr. Giark To You wrote:

MY>> I don't get what you mean. All you have to do is write:
MY>> A$="$VER: Programname 2.54"
MY>> at the very first line of your AMOS source code. This will do the
trick when
MY>> compiled.

MY> Where is this particular tidbit located? I've never seen that before.
Thanks.
MY> But, what about Set Buffer? The manual says that set buffer has to be
the
MY> first line (if you use it) And does it have to be A$?

No, of course not, $VER: isn't some 'special' string, it's normal string
like all other. All strings are located in one place in executabe file,
null-terminated, and $VER: is just one of them. It is advicable for it
to be first string defined (or used; same effect would have Print "$VER:
Programname 2.54" ), because of faster searching by Version command. But
if you, for instance, have some sort of About requester, and show $VER:
string in it, that would work fine also. Same thing works for C, asm, or
any other programming language.

Regards
--

Re: Compiler?

Tue Nov 25, 1997 3:32 pm
Peter Cahill <cahill4@iol.ie>


On 14-Aug-98, Mr. Giark To You wrote:
>From: "Mr. Giark To You" <giark@hicksville.ddns.org>

>On 13-Aug-98, Rune J. Keller wrote:
>>I don't get what you mean. All you have to do is write:
>>A$="$VER: Programname 2.54"
>>at the very first line of your AMOS source code. This will do the trick when
>>compiled.

>Where is this particular tidbit located? I've never seen that before. Thanks.
>But, what about Set Buffer? The manual says that set buffer has to be the
>first line (if you use it) And does it have to be A$?

It can be any$, all that version does is search for '$VER:' in the code,
and it just prints out what is in the code after, so if you have:
A$="$VER: Programname 2.54" in AMOS version will return Programname 2.54
it can be set ANYWHERE in the code, with any name, once it starts as '$VER:'

cya,

	Message #669 of 8176

(no subject)

Sun Aug 16, 1998 11:48 am
Phil Price <cb.price@ukonline.co.uk>


Amiga Central , (working Name) Online magazine, plans, and notes.
-----------------------------------------------------------------

Hello fellow amigans, following the recent departure of Cu-Amiga,
from the Amiga world :( Many users were getting annoyed that
their would only be 1 true Amiga magazine (100% Amiga). I was
hanging about on irc and too of my friends on #a51 (Barry Jack,
Anthony Sherrat) were having some sort of argument/conversation
about CU Amiga, or something. I said 'CuAmiga is dead' Ant ,
replied 'I know' :( Then the usual things about Amiga Format
followed, then I had a flash of inspiration (du-darr) and I
thought that, as my new boss said that I could have
www.(whatever).com, I said 'Hey why not et up our own online
magazine' every 1 on the channel was pretty exited, and ideas
flew about for about 15 mins or so. So then it was decided that
www.amigacentral.com would be set up, but various other net works
have used the name Amiga central, even though that is not their
URL (www.amicon.org) for example, and I don't want to get into
legal fight about the name, so could some one come up with a
name ? And that is how this whole project came into existence.

About AmigaCentral:
------------------

[]. Amiga central will be a NON-PROFIT (all donations are
gratefully accepted :)) organization, it will be free for
all who want to browse though it. Any money made will be
used for buying equipment, and paying for the server.
Any extra will be kept for if/when , Amiga central
expands.

[]. A sponsor will be needed, or, some other form of Amiga
companies to advertise, maybe like a yellow pages, style
thing, I don't know, but i know that a some form of funds
will be needed , for the cost of hosting the site, and
postage. (see later)

[]. AmigaCentral, Will be a online magazine, that will be
wither , monthly, or just, and archive of added information
I'm not sure what to do, but I think that monthly should
be better.

[]. I'm looking to have 20 full-time, actual members of
amigacentral, These Are:

1. Chief WebMaster / Boss [That's me]
2. Co. Webmaster / CO Boss
3. Maintainor (to look after the bits and bobs)
4. Head Technical/Serious Reviewer
5. Head Games Reviewer
6&7. Dept. Tech. / Game Reviewer.
8-20. General Writers and reviewers.

Their a a few requirements for these positions, they are,

1. You must LOVE the amiga
2. You are not looking to gain any money from this (it's
non profit remember)
3. That you live in the UK (sorry) This is because, if
and when companies send their goods to be reviewed, they
will first be sent to me (phil price) then i will send
them onto the others, who would like to review that
thing (s/w-h/w).
4. And that you must not spread / copy and of the software
you receive.
5. Determination & Commitment.

[]. I will make a series for templates ,at a later date, for
reviews, and news, etc.. that the reviewers can just
cut and paste there txt into it, if thy are not too
keen, on doing this, they can just send a .txt file to
me and I'll do this.

[]. The proposed sections are , in no order. (not real names,
they can be changed)

News
Games Previews
Games Reviews
Technical Pre.
Technical Re.
Serious Pre.
Serious Re.
Best Of Aminet
PD stuff
Gallery
Mod of The Month. (MED,XM, DBM, Also)
Readers Mail
Reader Questions (like help)
Tutorials (music, Creative, Programming etc..)
Resources.
Trial s/w For Download.

[] The Colour Scheme Will be Red , White and Greys, like the boing
ball, I need some 1 to do a real good logo, when the name is
decided, I'm a bit handy at the o'l graphics too so I shall,
make one and let you lot decide which is the best.

[]. Due to AmigaCentrals, nature, NO money is needed to get it off
the ground, so a 'demo' site can be set up for companies in a
matter of a couple of weeks.

[]. We need to pester, All Amiga Companies to make them aware of this
online magazine :)

Well I hope This has been a good read for you and that you can join,
you can all mail me at cb.price@..., for you to ask questions,
ideas, graphics, proposals, money :) ect.ect. Also Join #amigacentral,
On IRCNet, (irc.steath.net) and A meeting will take place every Sunday
(including this one) from 8:45 onwards.

Most important is deciding a name for us, so i can get it set up on
Monday. :)

Thanx Alot

Phil Price

PS. Spread This Message all about, every where :) And could some one post
this to amiga news groups please..... (comp.sys.amiga ect.) I'm not on news
but i stil what the messge spread

Well, not AGA oriented, but I did write a tutorial for the GUI extension that
covers:

Using GadToolsBox to create a GUI file
Using AMOS to make a GUI bank
Using GUI commands to:
Check for close
Use Help system
Use text gadgets, string gadgets, Checkbox gadgets, MX gadgets, ASL file
requesters, GadTools requesters
Use listviews
Proper Prefs files
Tooltypes from icons
simple encryption/decryption scheme

I expect it will probably be included in the next public beta of GUI.

	Message #717 of 8176 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

HaHA!

Sun Aug 23, 1998 12:58 am
"Mr. Giark To You" <giark@hicksville.ddns.org>


After a bit of fiddling, I've finally got it!

Except for when using locateapsystem (how often does anyone do that?), I have
managed to get ap to look in #one# directory for all configs. I've fixed the
interpreter_config.amos file and added a line to user-startup. Now ap doesn't
have fits looking for configs (works with gui compiler, too).

Unfortunately, part of it hinges on the 3+ wb.

How?

Assign S: AMOS_Pro:S/ Add

That tells the amiga that s in your amos dir is part of s:

The second part is the revamped int_conf.amos file. I'll upload if you think
its a useful item.

Well met and godspeed,
                      Giark

                                       giark@hicksville.ddns.org

	Message #718 of 8176 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

turboext

Sun Aug 23, 1998 2:44 am
Hakan Venderlof <grok@flashback.net>


*** I do this: ***

Installation process - AmosPro

1) Copy AMOSPro_TURBO_Plus.Lib to your APSystem Drawer.
2) Boot up and load AmosPro.
3) Select "Set Interpreter" from the menu.
4) Click on "Load default Configuration".
5) Click on "Loaded Extensions".
6) At line 12 type in :- "AMOSPro_TURBO_Plus.Lib" ,
omitting the quotes.
7) Click on "Save Configuration".


*** but when I try to restart AMOSPro program
says 'cannot load extension'...
What might be wrong?

----------------------------------------------------------------
 greets  grok@flashback.net  (or: grok@online.idg.se)
----------------------------------------------------------------


@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@

	Message #719 of 8176 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: turboext

Sun Aug 23, 1998 7:58 pm
"Mr. Giark To You" <giark@hicksville.ddns.org>


On 22-Aug-98, Hakan Venderlof wrote:
>1) Copy AMOSPro_TURBO_Plus.Lib to your APSystem Drawer.
>2) Boot up and load AmosPro.
>3) Select "Set Interpreter" from the menu.
>4) Click on "Load default Configuration".
>5) Click on "Loaded Extensions".
>6) At line 12 type in :- "AMOSPro_TURBO_Plus.Lib" ,
> omitting the quotes.
>7) Click on "Save Configuration".
>*** but when I try to restart AMOSPro program
> says 'cannot load extension'...
> What might be wrong?

Remember that message I sent about fixing the interpreter config? This is why.
Amos pro, as is, stores the interpreter_config in 3 places. Without using the
fix, you have to save the interpreter config (note that the unfixed version
does not even give you the proper name as default) in three separate places.
s:, AMOSPro_System:, APSystem.

I've patched the interpreter_config.amos program to make it all look in the
same place all the time.

Well met and godspeed,
                      Giark
                                             ICQ 12235820
                                       giark@hicksville.ddns.org
                                http://www.hicksville.ddns.org/~erotica/

--cut--
Curs Off : Flash Off
'
' Initialize text and zones
'
Reserve Zone 4
FH=8 : Rem font height
XO=120 : YO=80
Ink 0
Restore OPTIONS
For I=1 To 4
Read T$
YG=YO+(I-1)*FH
Text XO,YG+Text Base,T$
Set Zone I,XO,YG To XO+Text Length(T$),YG+FH-1
Next
'
' Wait for mouse click on option
'
Repeat
Z=Mouse Zone
If Z
YG=YO+(Z-1)*FH
Ink 0,2
Restore OPTIONS
For I=1 To Z : Read T$ : Next
Text XO,YG+Text Base,T$
Repeat
If Mouse Click : Cls : Print "You clicked ";T$ : Exit 2 : End If
Until Mouse Zone<>Z
Ink 0,1
Text XO,YG+Text Base,T$
End If
Until Mouse Click
'
Direct
'
OPTIONS:
Data "Option 1","Option 2","Option 3","Option 4"
--cut--

Re: Converting AMOS to Visual BASIC

Wed Aug 26, 1998 3:58 pm
"Garfield Benjamin" <gbenjam@sosbbs.com>


> A friend has written some programs using AMOS on his Amiga
> systems. Has anyone had any experience converting AMOS code to
> Visual BASIC (or even Visual C++)? I'm not concerned about having
> to do some manual translations, but I am mainly concerned about
> emulating the console I/O, sound, and graphic capabilities of AMOS,
> perhaps something that uses DirectSound and DirectDraw.

Is there some reason why the conversion needs to perfromed with
VC++ or VB?

It should be very simple to convert the AMOS programs to C &
Allegro. As I have said before, Allegro is an excellent audio-video
library.

First, it's reasonably fast: my bob routines can handle around 300
64w X 26h animated bobs in 1 Vbl, even on my P133. Keep in mind
that a VGA Vbl occurs 70fps and you will realize just how fast the
bob drawing is.

Second, it's very easy to use!!

The bob demo is available from my PC page and a vertically
scrolling shooter is available from my GAMES page... both are
written in C & Allegro.

	Message #746 of 8176 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

The mad GUI Compiler :) (..was Compiler Woes)

Wed Aug 26, 1998 9:02 pm
Pietro Ghizzoni <ghizzo@agonet.it>


Hello Mr.

On 25-Ago-98, Mr. Giark To You wrote: [amos-list] Re: Compiler Woes

> From: "Mr. Giark To You" <giark@hicksville.ddns.org>
>
> On 25-Aug-98, Dale Hymanyk wrote:
>> The program uses just AMOSPro2 and Gui ext commands with a few Ldos ones
>> thrown in, but these always compiled fine in my pre-Gui programs.
>
> Are you using wait? There are several commands that no longer work when
> compiled with the gui version of the compiler.


There is confusion.... i'll explain better the GUI Compiler in the future docs
:)


All the GUI Compiler users should read this......


1- *You don't need the GUI Compiler for your GUI Ext. programs!* ...you can
use
the standard AMOSPro compiler without problem. The GUI Extension is a
standard AMOSPro v2 Extension, and so it works fine with the AMOSPro compiler
too.

*2- If you use the GUI compiler ALL the amos commands works without problem.*
*But anyway see belove...*


so.... what does the GUI compiler? what's the difference? The main difference
between the GUI and AMOSPro compiler is that the compiled code generated by
the GUI compiler hides all the AMOS bullshits in the code. If you zap the code
you'll not see nothing AMOS related... if you zap the code generated by the
standard AMOSPro compiler, you'll find tons of AMOS
stuffs like the name of all the amos extensions installed in your system and
other preferences.

If you trace a AMOS compiled program using snoopdos or other programs, you'll
notice other AMOS activities, like search and freeze the other running AMOS
programs, searh the misterious AMOS_Switcher and other stuff. Well... the GUI
Compiler remove these "unuseful" operations as well.

If you run a virus checker togheter AMOS, it will probably pop up a warning
message because some system functions has been modified... for experts:

- Graphics.library LoadView() ... only on AGA machine
- Intuition.library EasyRequestArgs()
- Intuition.library AutoRequest()

these has been also removed.


So essentially the GUI compiler:

- hides the AMOS rubbish in the code

- makes your AMOS programs able to run in multitasknig with the other AMOS
programs! As you know you can't run 2 o more AMOS programs togheter, because
only the last one will run while the others will be freezed. Now you can!

- makes your programs more "clean" and virus checkers warnings free :)))


Since so many AMOS stuffs has been removed from the code, is not a good idea
use it in AMOS games for example... the GUI compiler is specifically designed
for *workbench applications only.* If your program run in the WB enviroment,
it doesn't needs all the amos patches and hacks, for this reason i've created
the
GUI Compiler!

If you need to open AMOS screens and related stuffs , use the AMOSPro
compiler.

If you need a nice workbench GUI for your programs, use the GUI compiler.


About the commands that doesn't works anymore.... this isn't a GUI Compiler
effect... this happen if you put the Gui Amiga 1 command at the start of your
program. What does Gui Amiga 1, and why some commands doesn't works anymore???

Simple... the Gui Amiga 1 command disable other AMOS internal functions in
order to makes your program a bit more os friendly. In paticular, this command
remove the AMOS interrupt routine!!!!!! So all the vbl/interrupt based
commands/functions doesn't works!! Mainly:

- Music
- Samples
- AMAL
- vbl commands and timer
- amos gfx

if you're creating a WB program, usually you don't need the above stuffs, and
so is a good idea to disable them.

Anyway if you need them (.. for example Music and sample)
*don't call Gui Amiga 1 and everything will works as usual! * Therefore i
suggest you to use other
extensions for music and sample, because the AMOS music extension is really
bad coded!

I hope that now the GUI Compiler target is clear :)

---

Bye!

Amos.library upgrade (for AMOSPro v2)

Thu Aug 27, 1998 7:45 pm
Pietro Ghizzoni <ghizzo@agonet.it>


Hi!

Just today i've finished to modify some code in the amos.library. Due to the
several reports about my previous release and the related problem, i've
decided to totally trash the F.Lionet code used in the amos/workbench flip
routine, and
rewrite it in a more OS friendly way. Now the flip code is twice fast :)

It's more intelligent.... maybe someone remember the little and boring
intuition screen
opened by the old AMOS The Creator programs..... Europress has claimed that
with AMOSPro the screen has been removed..... false!! It's just hidden! It's
opened when amos is in front (.. so you don't see it) and it's immediately
closed when amos goes to back.

Now it's died forever, and a more efficient flip method has been implemented.
The interlace problem with AmigaOS 3.1 is fixed also....

Test it, flip several time between amos and the wb, and tell me that it works
fine or i'll kill you! :)
Hold down the Amiga-A keys for a while and enjoy the new flip speed.

--


Bye!

Re: Where can I get Allegro?

Thu Aug 27, 1998 9:06 pm
"Garfield Benjamin" <gbenjam@sosbbs.com>


> Where can I get Allegro? Is it a stand-alone language or
> a library/extension pack for C+ or some other language?

Sorry for the delay in replying...

Allegro is a **FREE** library for use with C or C++, specifically
Allegro is for use with the **FREE** DJGPP compiler!!

The url for the Allegro website is:
http://www.talula.demon.co.uk/allegro/index.html

If you are interested in EASY, POWERFUL PC programming then
I highly recommend DJGPP and Allegro. C/C++ are so easy and
powerful by themselves and adding in the Allegro audio-video
support results in one fantastic development system.


             Garfield Benjamin    e-mail:gbenjam@sosbbs.com
                  Website( http://www.sosbbs.com/~gbenjam )

	Message #767 of 8176 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: Amos + Free Memory

Fri Aug 28, 1998 3:41 pm
"Mr. Giark To You" <giark@hicksville.ddns.org>


On 28-Aug-98, Declan Gorman wrote:
>Is there any way in AmosPro to tell how much free memory a user has.

Exec "Avail >RAM:memory.txt"
Set Input 10,-1
Open In 1,"RAM:memory.txt"
Input #1,A$
Input #1,CHP$
Input #1,FST$
Close 1
Set Input 10,13
A$=Left$(CHP$,16)
B$=Right$(A$,12)
CHP=Val(B$)
A$=Left$(FST$,16)
B$=Right$(A$,12)
FST=Val(B$)

This will give you the current amount of CHIP and FAST ram available. You can
also parse the lines to get the total CHIP and FAST on the machine.

You could also use the A=Chip Free and A=Fast Free commands.

Well met and godspeed,
                      Giark
                                             ICQ 12235820
                                       giark@hicksville.ddns.org
                                http://www.hicksville.ddns.org/~erotica/

	Message #769 of 8176 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: Hello! out There!

Fri Aug 28, 1998 4:19 pm
"Rune J. Keller" <keller@vip.cybercity.dk>


On 28-Aug-98, John Glanville wrote:
> Hey does Ne1 know how 2 change RGB to RRGGBB.... Not using an extension?
> As I need more acuracy with colour.... Especially when grabbing a 256 colour
workbench screen from AmosPro! Hey is Ne1 else out there more into the
Graphics side of programming like me!
> And does Ne1 have a quick way of remapping an Images colours!
> Thanx 4 listening!

RGB=$59c

R=RGB/256
G=(RGB/16) mod 16
B=RGB mod 16

RRGGBB=B*16+G*16*256+R*16*256*256

Is this what you want?

	Message #771 of 8176

Re: Converting AMOS to Visual BASIC

Fri Aug 28, 1998 2:58 pm
Francesco De Napoli <zokie@teseo.it>


Hello Greg

On 24-Ago-98, Greg Larson wrote:
> From: "Greg Larson" <greenfuzz@earthlink.net>
>
> Hello,
>
> A friend has written some programs using AMOS on his Amiga systems. Has
> anyone had any experience converting AMOS code to Visual BASIC (or even
> Visual C++)? I'm not concerned about having to do some manual
> translations, but I am mainly concerned about emulating the console
I/O,
> sound, and graphic capabilities of AMOS, perhaps something that uses
> DirectSound and DirectDraw.

Many yaers ago, with a friend of mine I had developed about 20 educatiol
videogames/programs for a teacher. We think to sell them to other schools,
but they want them on PC only, but ridiculous thing was that they haven't
a PC, and Commodore wasn't dead!

So we investigate how to port them into VB. We buy a lot of M$ VB books,
after bulk headaches, I decide to avoid it like plague. Now my friend is
writing that kind of program in VB, they are bulk, plenty of bugs, needs
PII, but they are easy to sell. Programms that we wrote in AMOS were more
user-friendly, and child like them much more newst ones! Even if they had
32
Color graphic, and under Win95 they had 800x600 24Bit graphic
(to avoid palette problem).

When I say him of next AMOS-like language that is under development, he
was very happy and hope it will be ported even on PC. Pietro, what do you
think about? On PC there are many Development tools & language, but
none is so powerful and userfriendly like AMOS :) I think it will be a
successful product.

VB is great to do Access Interface or report, but to develope other kind
of software, i.e. little videogames, is a bad tool. It is full of strange
bugs and nonsense. But you may use OCX (like VC++) to use sprite, sound,
or other things that you need. There are a lot of OCX to do everything
(form control a coffe machine to virtual sex), but you need to buy them ;)
OCX is a M$'s technolgy for plug-in. You may use OCX with all language
that support them.

I think your friend should use C++ (on PC VC++ is a must, so you can
easily use Microsoft Foundation Classes :(), so he
ought develope classes to emulate AMOS command, so porting will be more
easy, but it is difficult to do this job, but not impossible. He should
know well how use C++ & DirectX.
The marvellous thing on VC++ is that old example don't compile on newest
release. This a M$ 100% compliant product :) VB5.0 often can't compile
VB4.0 source, and soon as possible will be release VB6.0 for Win98, so
will be newest funny problem with old sources :)

OFFTOPIC
IF you want good book on C++ or Java, goto http://www.BruceEckel.com/
You will find: Thinking in C++ 2nd edition (alpha6) (RTF & TXT) and
Thinking in JAVA (pdf). This are commercial books, but Bruce give them for
free on internet, so there is much more debugging before pubblishing them,
uhhh like M$ :-)))

--
"When do you want to reboot today?"

On 28-Aug-98, Scooter D. Matott sXe wrote:
>> You could also use the A=Chip Free and A=Fast Free commands.
>no kidding you could, what was all that other stuff for, giark?

Chip/Fast Free give *only* the amount currently usable. Using Avail gives more
info on memory than the AMOS commands, say if you wanted to make a slider bar
of available/used memory.

Did you ever notice that, even though =Fast Free will tell you how much
memory, even if you have >8Mb, the memory gauge at the top of the screen does
not work if you have more than 8Mb?
