	Message #788 of 8176 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: snow

Mon Aug 31, 1998 3:59 pm
"Garfield Benjamin" <gbenjam@sosbbs.com>


> Hm has someone got a code for a 'snowfall'
> preferably where snow slowly builds up in bottom of screen...?

Sure, I made a "Christmas Demo" a few years back which does
exactly that... snow falls and lands on the text (Merry Christmas)
and background scenery (trees, etc).

I wrote it in BLITZ, but it would be simple to convert to AMOS.

Actually, all you need to do for an AMOS Snow Demo is:
----------<START OF CODE>----------
NUMFLKS=99
Dim SNOWXPOS(NUMFLKS), SNOWYPOS(NUMFLKS)
Dim SNOWYSPD(NUMFLKS)

Rem Define procedures...
Procedure CLEAR_SNOW
For REP=0 To NUMFLKS
Rem where 0=Background
Plot SNOWXPOS(REP), SNOWYPOS(REP), 0
Next REP
End Proc

Procedure UPDATE_SNOW
Shared REALSCRN, COLSCRN
For REP=0 To NUMFLKS
XSPD=Rnd(4)-2 : YSPD=Rnd(4)+1
SNOWXPOS(REP)=SNOWXPOS(REP)+XSPD
SNOWYPOS(REP)=SNOWYPOS(REP)+YSPD
Rem We have the new position, now check for collision...
Screen COLSCRN
TEST=Point( SNOWXPOS(REP), SNOWYPOS(REP) )
Screen REALSCRN
If ( TEST <> 0 ) : Rem where 0=Background color
Rem Ahh, the snow has landed!!
Rem So, we reset this snowflake...
SNOWX(REP)=Rnd(352)
SNOWY(REP)=0
Else
Rem SNOWCOLOR is the color register you're using for the
Rem snow. In my demo, I used YSPD and had a range of
Rem colors from white to a bluish grey. This makes a very
Rem nice effect when the snow builds up.
Plot SNOWXPOS(REP), SNOWYPOS(REP), SNOWCOLOR
End If
Next REP
End Proc

Rem Initialize the snow...
For REP=0 To NUMFLKS
SNOWX(REP)=Rnd(352)
SNOWY(REP)=-(REP*3) : Rem Note the - sign
Next REP

Rem Create two screens... REAL is buffered, COL is not...
REALSCRN=0 : COLSCRN=1
Screen Open REALSCRN, 320, 240, 64, Lowres
Double Buffer : Autoback 0 : Bob Update Off
Screen Open COLSCRN, 320, 240, 64, Lowres
Autoback 0 : Bob Update Off : Screen Hide COLSCRN

Rem Initialize the screen palettes and load the IFF picture into
Rem REALSCRN. Draw all static images into REALSCRN then...
Screen Copy Logic(REALSCRN) To Physic(COLSCRN)

Finally, we are ready for the action...

ALL_DONE=False
Timer=0
Repeat
CLEAR_SNOW
UPDATE_SNOW
If Fire(0) Then ALL_DONE=True
If Timer>1200 Then ALL_DONE=True
Screen Swap REALSCRN : Wait Vbl
Until ALL_DONE

Fade 5 : Wait 75
End
----------<END OF CODE>----------

It's been a while since I have used AMOS and I'm actually creating
this program "on the fly" in this e-mail, so there may be errors.

The basic idea is covered here and that should put you well on your
way.


             Garfield Benjamin    e-mail:gbenjam@sosbbs.com
                  Website( http://www.sosbbs.com/~gbenjam )


@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@

	Message #789 of 8176

Re: snow

Mon Aug 31, 1998 4:11 pm
"Garfield Benjamin" <gbenjam@sosbbs.com>


Arrgh!! See, I said there may be errors!!

Replace the UPDATE_SNOW procedure with this one...

Procedure UPDATE_SNOW
Shared REALSCRN, COLSCRN
For REP=0 To NUMFLKS
XSPD=Rnd(4)-2 : YSPD=Rnd(4)+1
TESTXPOS=SNOWXPOS(REP)+XSPD
TESTYPOS=SNOWYPOS(REP)+YSPD
Rem We have the new position, now check for collision...
Screen COLSCRN
TEST=Point( TESTXPOS, TESTYPOS )
Screen REALSCRN
If ( TEST <> 0 ) : Rem where 0=Background color
Rem Ahh, the snow has landed!!
Plot SNOWXPOS(REP), SNOWYPOS(REP), SNOWCOLOR
Rem So, we reset this snowflake...
SNOWXPOS(REP)=Rnd(352)
SNOWYPOS(REP)=0
Else
SNOWXPOS(REP)=TESTXPOS
SNOWYPOS(REP)=TESTYPOS
Rem SNOWCOLOR is the color register you're using for the
Rem snow. In my demo, I used YSPD and had a range of
Rem colors from white to a bluish grey. This makes a very
Rem nice effect when the snow builds up.
Plot SNOWXPOS(REP), SNOWYPOS(REP), SNOWCOLOR
End If
Next REP
End Proc


I had a fatal error in that the snow would never accumulate. This is
fixed now. Also fixed two label references which were inaccurate.

Anyway, I am done with this, gotta go, but I hope it all helps!!


             Garfield Benjamin    e-mail:gbenjam@sosbbs.com
                  Website( http://www.sosbbs.com/~gbenjam )

	Message #791 of 8176 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Magazine views of AMOS

Wed Dec 31, 1969 11:59 pm
"Alastair Murray" <malcolm.murray@virgin.net>


I think the problem with the magazine (and general) views of AMOS is
that they don't realise what is made in it.

There are a lot of bad programmers who use AMOS because it is easy and
produce games that are poor and look AMOS like. This is what the
magazines see.

When a game made in AMOS is good, you can't even tell it is made in
AMOS and no-one says a thing. They only notice the bad software.

Both CU and AF regularly have all sorts of AMOS programs on their
coverdisks, often as the main program of the month, they don't even
know it!

They just have a general lack of knowledge about how AMOS has moved on
through extensions.

I can't blame them for not liking it as it does has its problems, what
I do think is strange is the way they recomend Blitz when it has many
of the same problems and a lot more besides.

-Murray
